  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_72d739b5-0483-4d94-b5ad-8203575d9e3b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer13634722480854447090"><b>In the real world, when you vanish into thin air for a week, people tend to notice. </b><br/><br/>After his unexpected journey into the lands of the fey, Ethan Chase just wants to get back to normal.   <span id="freeText13634722480854447090" style="display:none"><b>In the real world, when you vanish into thin air for a week, people tend to notice. </b><br /><br />After his unexpected journey into the lands of the fey, Ethan Chase just wants to get back to normal. Well, as "normal" as you can be when you see faeries every day of your life. Suddenly the former loner with the bad reputation has someone to try for-his girlfriend, Kenzie. Never mind that he's forbidden to see her again. <br /><br />But when your name is Ethan Chase and your sister is one of the most powerful faeries in the Nevernever, "normal" simply isn't to be. For Ethan's nephew, Keirran, is missing, and may be on the verge of doing something unthinkable in the name of saving his own love. Something that will fracture the human and faery worlds forever, and give rise to the dangerous fey known as the Forgotten. As Ethan's and Keirran's fates entwine and Keirran slips further into darkness, Ethan's next choice may decide the fate of them all.</span>

  <blockquote>My name is Ethan Chase. <br/>Just shy of a week ago, I was dr</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9792332408087524451" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494356530ra/22707828.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, that ending..... are you serious right now? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494356530ra/22707829.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, lets move away from that for a minute and let me crack on with it. <br><br><b>First:</b> This cover is freaking amazing! I'm totally freaking in love with it. ❤ That is Keirran on the front and he's making it look even better - BUT - I want to kick him from one end of Nevernever to the other end! <br><br>Let me add an excerpt that you might not want to read because of **spoilers** from the other books. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>My name is Ethan Chase. <br>Just shy of a week ago, I was dragged into Faeryland. <br>Again. <br>The first time it happened, I was four. Yeah, four years old, kidnapped by faeries and taken into the Nevernever, home of the fey. Long story short, my older sister rescued me and brought me home, but became a faery queen herself and now rules a part of the Nevernever called the Iron Realm. <br><br>Thirteen years later, despite all the precautions I took against the Fair Folk, it happened again. I found myself smack-dab in the middle of Nevernever, and this time I wasn't alone. A classmate of mine, a girl named Mackenzie St. James, managed to get pulled in, as well. A lot of weird, screwed-up stuff happened in the next few days, like following a talking cat through Nevernever, meeting my sister in the Iron Realm, sneaking out of the Iron Realm to meet up with the Queen of the Exiles and, oh yeah, discovering that my sister has a son. That's right, I have a nephew. A nephew who is part fey, completely unknown to my parents, and who, by the way of screwy faery time, is the same age as me.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So, Keirran is in love with Annwyl who is exiled from the Summer Court and she's fading away. Long story, read the book. Keirran is running all around trying to find a cure. <br><br>Then Ethan gets involved because he wants to help Annwyl and of course Kenzie comes along which isn't a good idea because she has an illness. I love Kenzie though, she has a lot of spunk. <br><br>Anyway, they do this that the other and what not and we end up with me wanting to kill the Summer Queen, Titania. I have always hated her. We have some guest appearances from Meghan, Ash, Grim and Puck. We have some evil things called the Forgotton, as there are always evil things in these books popping up left and right. And we have some deaths!<br><br>There you have it people! The book rocks even though there is a massive amount of stupidity and I hope it all gets better in the last book!<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/05/the-iron-traitor-by-julie-kagawa.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_615007505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615007505" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615007505?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781460321010" href="/book/show/18510457-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=beta-male">beta-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=b-word-heroine">b-word-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=tstl-male">tstl-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615007505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1970303098749848667">I know that not all children turn out to be like their parents, but man, that Keirran is something else. It's the equivalent of Bill and Hillary Clinton having Justin Bieber as a son.<br/><br/><b>Judge me how you will, but not since Harry Potter #5 have my feelings been so heightened by the events of a book.</b> I want to punch someone (Keirran). I want to yell at him. I want to pick him up and shake some goddamn sense into him. I want to hold Annwyl's hand and stay with her into that sad goodnight. I want to sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1970303098749848667" style="display:none">I know that not all children turn out to be like their parents, but man, that Keirran is something else. It's the equivalent of Bill and Hillary Clinton having Justin Bieber as a son.<br><br><b>Judge me how you will, but not since Harry Potter #5 have my feelings been so heightened by the events of a book.</b> I want to punch someone (Keirran). I want to yell at him. I want to pick him up and shake some goddamn sense into him. I want to hold Annwyl's hand and stay with her into that sad goodnight. I want to shake some sense into Kenzie. I want to pull Ethan in for a hug and never let him go. I am so angry. I am so upset. I just finished reading this book not 15 minutes ago, and truly, my feels are all over the place.<br><br>I have always loved Julie Kagawa's Iron Fey series, but I don't think ever been so emotionally invested in a book within this series as much as I have been with this one. I <i>really liked</i> the Iron Fey. I enjoyed previous book in the <i>Call of the Forgotten</i> series. I can say with absolutely certainty that <i>I love this book</i> and <b>I consider it one of the best YA novels I've read all year</b>. Love, sacrifice, adventure, old friends, new enemies; you've got it all within the pages in this book. Yes, the end has me shrieking in horror. It is a cliffhanger of the heartwrenching sort. <b>I will take that cliffhanger, I will take all the horror and upset and anger it has wreaked in my emotions, and I will say to Ms. Kagawa, <i>"Please, miss, may I have some more?"</i></b> It is a good sort of pain.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383457261ra/6566878.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Summary</u>: Ethan and Kenzie are back home, and in a shit ton of trouble with their respective parents. Kenzie winds up in the hospital because of her cancer, Ethan's in a ton of trouble with his parents. Suddenly, Ethan gets a special visit from his sister---it turns out that Keirran, Meghan's son and Ethan's nephew, has gone missing. Soon after, Ethan gets more visits from the fae, some unwanted, some welcome, but altogether unexpected. Before he knows it, Ethan is pulled unwillingly into yet another adventure, because like it or not, Keirran is family, and he's going to do what he can to find him.<br><br>Keirran is a man on a mission. Annwyl, his love, is Fading, and he will do anything to stop it. It's the fae version of death. She is slowly physically disappearing, and her memories are fading away as well. It is all she can do to keep hanging on in order to say goodbye to Keirran before it's too late. However, Keirran is desperate, and what he is willing to wager for Annwyl's life will endanger more than they can ever imagine.<br><br><u>The setting &amp; plot</u>: The story is fast-paced, action-packed, but never at the cost of characterization. There are slow moments, tender moments, introspection, but not for a single moment did this book lose my attention. <b>It has been a long time since a book has captured my attention so thoroughly from beginning to end.</b> The setting is beautiful, well-described. It takes us to the Goblin Market in New Orleans, to the Between, to the Nevernever, to Summer, to Tir na Nog and the frigidly beautiful land of Winter. Deceptively beautiful, that is, because nothing is ever guileless in the land of the Fae.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Bees and butterflies floated everywhere among the flowers, sparkling like living jewels, and I could feel the sun’s warmth beating down on us. Everything looked peaceful, but I knew what a horrible lie that was in Faery. If everything appeared this tranquil, there was probably something stupidly dangerous lurking nearby.</i>
</blockquote>The creatures and the setting is typical Kagawa, which is to say, evocative, beautiful, brilliant. <b>For me, a book has to have a combination of a compelling plot and complex characters, and this book has everything I could ever want.</b><br><br><u>The Characters</u>: <b>I loved how Ethan and Keirran's situations turn out to ever-so-subtly parallel one another</b>. Both Ethan and Keirran's loves are dying---Kenzie growing weaker by the day from cancer, Annwyl Fading out of existence. The difference is in their characters, and how they each individually react to their situation.<br><br>I was not overly fond of Ethan in the last book. I mean, I liked him in the way one would tolerate a headstrong, annoying sibling who grew up into a sullen, angry young man who pushed everyone away, but Ethan's character took a change for the better in this sequel. <b>Ethan is so much more mature this time around, and I loved him for it.</b> Ethan is <i>trying</i> so hard to break out of his shell. He wants to be a good son who doesn't worry his parents, he wants to be a good boyfriend to Kenzie. He is so loyal, and it hurts me to see his loyalty put to the test, and so severely abused by his nephew, Keirran. Unlike Keirran, who is willing to throw away everything in the name of love, Ethan is more levelheaded. Even when it comes to his beloved Kenzie and her own fight against the cancer that might be killing her.<br><blockquote>
  <i>I wish I could, I thought, closing my eyes. I wish there was some way, some bargain or deal or contract, to make you well again, but I know the rules. Nothing is free. Magic and power always come with a price. And maybe that’s selfish and paranoid, but I’m not willing to pay that price, or have you pay that price. Not yet. Not when there’s still a chance you could be okay without it.</i>
</blockquote>Ethan knows loss, and he is willing to put up with loss, because Ethan knows some prices are higher than he is willing to pay. Damn it, Ethan. <b>You are this close to being my 4th book boyfriend, and this feels so wrong, considering I've watched you grow up from a scared little 5-year old boy.</b> I don't want to be a pedophile ;_;<br><br>I have a love/hate relationship with Keirran. Let's get one thing straight, I love his character while hating him. <b>It is one thing to despise a character for his actions while still being able to appreciate his complexity, his impulses, his motivations, and I understand and sympathize with Keirran, even if I cannot overlook his contemptible behavior in the name of love.</b> Keirran is in a lot of pain. He is his father's son, through and through, and I kind of went "awwww" at the little father-son moment of bonding within the book. Keirran is haunted.<br><blockquote>
  <i>...as the hooded figure spun, his cloak swirling around him. My stomach lurched as our gazes met. Cold ice-blue eyes stabbed at me from beneath the hood, and bright silver hair fell around his face, the only spots of color to be seen. Beneath the cloak, he was dressed in black: black shirt, pants, boots, even gloves. I remembered the smiling, easygoing faery from just a week ago. The hard-eyed creature dressed all in black, staring at me in this den of shadow and fear, seemed like a stranger.</i>
</blockquote>He is driven almost insane by desperation in his quest to save Annwyl. So many times within this book, I found myself wanting to scream with frustration at Keirran and his foolhardiness. Ethan was right. Keirran will pay "any price" for Annwyl's life, and really, it's just too much. The boy cannot see beyond himself and his wishes.<br><br>Annwyl herself is so much stronger than Keirran. I adored her. She is deceptively soft, gentle, lovely as a gentry of a Summer court Fae should be. <b>However, underneath Annwyl's fragile, ethereal appearance lies a backbone of pure steel.</b> Annwyl knows what Kierran is willing to pay for her life, and she knows better. She does not want to be the cause of such sacrifice, and she would much prefer to Fade away in peace. She stands up to Keirran, despite Keirran's inability to actually fucking LISTEN to what she wants.<blockquote>
  <i>“I am standing right here, Keirran,” Annwyl said, sounding angrier than I’d ever heard before. Her green eyes flashed as she stared the prince down. “And I did not ask you to save me if it meant bargaining at the goblin market, making deals that could get you killed and running away from the Prince Consort of Mag Tuiredh. You did not ask me what I felt about this plan—you just disappeared without telling anyone.”</i>
</blockquote>Old friends make an appearance in this novel. <b>We meet Grimalkin, Robin Goodfellow, etc. again, but they do not play a major role in the book, and I completely agree with that.</b> This is not their book. This is not their story. As much as I love them, Grim, Puck, etc. are part of Meghan and Ash's crowd. This is Ethan and Keirran's book. This is a new generation. Grim and Puck help things along, but they are not major characters, nor do I expect them to be. Their presence in the book was delightful, unexpected, and <b>just right</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <i>...two golden eyes blinked into existence, regarding us lazily.<br>We leaped to our feet, and Grimalkin yawned, raising a hind foot to scratch an ear. “Hello again, humans,” the cat purred, as Razor screeched a loud “Bad kitty!” that made Keirran wince. “Still getting into trouble, I see.”</i>
</blockquote>You will never hear me say this again, but <b>Ash is a total DILF</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383457947ra/6567069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jesus Christ. Yeah, I know he's with Meghan. And I love them together. But I can't help myself...when he made his cameo in the story, I shrieked like the most undignified fangirl ever. It was hilarious to see Keirran literally running away and hiding from his father's wrath. Given the father or the son, Ash always wins.<br><blockquote>
  <i>A silhouette was striding down the center of the road, heading for the alley we’d just vacated. Lean, tall, a long black coat rippling behind him, he was instantly recognizable. Even from this distance, I could see the glow of his sword, blue-black and deadly, and the glint of a cold silver eye.</i>
</blockquote>I'm so desperate for the next book, you cannot even imagine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1970303098749848667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442065394?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chester Carstairs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chester Carstairs" href="/user/show/5705811-chester-carstairs">Chester Carstairs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19100586-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442065394" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10610449825842169090">Damn, Julie Kagawa has done it yet again! Oh, when will I ever stop putting myself through this author's miserable world? That freaking ending. I mean, what. the. hell.<br/><br/>Our beloved Kenzie and Ethan are back in the human world. For a short while, at least. Then Meghan showed up claiming Keirran is missing, a certain Thin Man is following Ethan, and the most worrisome of all... a Fading Annwyl.<br/><br/>This has been another crazy ride. We were taken into the Between, back to the wyldwood and even get to rev</span>
  <span id="freeText10610449825842169090" style="display:none">Damn, Julie Kagawa has done it yet again! Oh, when will I ever stop putting myself through this author's miserable world? That freaking ending. I mean, what. the. hell.<br /><br />Our beloved Kenzie and Ethan are back in the human world. For a short while, at least. Then Meghan showed up claiming Keirran is missing, a certain Thin Man is following Ethan, and the most worrisome of all... a Fading Annwyl.<br /><br />This has been another crazy ride. We were taken into the Between, back to the wyldwood and even get to revisit Arcadia and Tir Na Nog! Yep. :D<br /><br />Also, let's not forget that we got a certain favorite character back for a longer time! I so missed his wickedness. Sorry ice-boy, but this raven will always have my heart.<br /><br />Well, there's still the never-ending cheesy lines from our two couples, that sometimes... well ALWAYS make me roll my eyes, but hey, they're cute!<br /><br />The ending, though... how about we don't talk about the ending at all?</span>

  <span id="freeText12581171710741771458" style="display:none">So apparently I wrote this long lost reaction as soon I finished reading the book. And oh boy <i>did I laugh at myself</i> for being so emotional. So enjoy reading a emotional wreak's reaction, my fellow readers. <br><br><b>WHAT IN THE NAME OF FUCKERY FUCK WAS THAT?</b> <br>I want to bitch slap Keirran so hard that he will feel the antagonizing pain deep in his coal black soul.<br>And then I want to bitch slap Titania so hard that she will forever be banished like that flunkee should have been centuries ago.<br>And then I want to bitch slap the Forgotten Queen so hard that she will be famously known for my infamous bitch slap.<br>And then I want to bitch slap any random person who will walking past me because they can't understand the pain I am going through right now as of this moment.<br><br>I want to curl myself up on my bed and cry out my feels for a thousand years.<br>I want Puck to hug me forever because I am all alone here suffering from this disaster called the <b>fucking ending.</b><br>There are Winter, Summer and Iron courts. Where the hell is the Heartbroken court? Because I sure as hell will be the queen of that. <br>I want to trade with the sneaky goblins that I want the next book now. They can have my heart. It's already <i>fucking broken into tiny little bits and pieces.</i><br>You think this is a joke Julie Kagawa? Eh? Because I don't see a trip to Never-land after the last page of this merciless book. I hate and love you so much. Ugh.<br><br>And what a little <b>piece of shit</b> Keirran is. I am actually sad for Ash. That imbecile son of yours knows no limits. You will certainly see me clapping behind with encouragement while Ash will be punishing him in the next book hopefully. I will even volunteer for a kick or two. (maybe four plus a punch)<br>You know what's the difference between you and daddy Ash, Keirran? Ash has a very critical organ known as the brain you fucktard. You are not just an Iron traitor. No. You are a fan girl traitor. And that's worse. I wanted to love you because you are Ash's blood. But no. You had to turnout to be a dumb fuck. <br><br>Ethan. Baby. I just started loving you. Don't you dare die on me. <br><b>Pretty please. Summer fey made hot lava cake with rare delicious ice cream straight off from the depths of the Ice Land and iron made digestible colorful sprinkles please.</b><br><br>I hate waiting. I can't wait. I am done. Wake me up when the next book is in my hands. *gets off the chair and hides under the blanket with all the feels and unconditional love for Julie Kagawa*<br><br>---<br>Previous review:<br><b> OH MY GOD.   <i>"how entangled my life would soon become with his,and how he would be the catalyst..for the end of everything"</i>

I still don't get why Ethan hates Ash. I mean seriously who in their right mind would hate Ash<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381529837ra/4988080.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Ohhh..and I was screaming my head off whenever <b>ASH, Meghan and Puck</b> was being </span>
  <span id="freeText6005374962271085653" style="display:none"><b>AFTER READING THE BOOK:</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>"how entangled my life would soon become with his,and how he would be the catalyst..for the end of everything"</i>
</b><br><br><br>When I read that line I knew without a doubt that Kierran would do something stupid.<br><br>Although, I was terrified of reading this book,I'm actually surprised that I liked Ethan and Kenzie here. I still don't get why Ethan hates Ash. My heart actually stopped whenever the names of those three were mentioned. <br><br><br>Overall the story is GREAT..even though I wanted to do bad things to a certain character in the end of the book I'm actually eager and terrified for the next book.<br><br><br><br>______________________________________________________________<br><br>Now, I don't want to jump into any conclusions,but the ending in the last book..and Kierran saying those things about the Forgotten.ARRRGHHHHH!!!<b>If this traitor <u>IS</u> Kierran, I'm gonna do this to HIM</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br><br>Because seriously???After reading the first book I was like <b>"did he really come from Meghan and Ash"??</b> Because I think his bad news..and that he lost his brains somewhere along talking to the Forgotten Queen,or maybe even before that!!!!!!!<br><br><br><b>
  <i>UPDATE:</i>

<div id="review_581913810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581913810" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581913810?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210916" href="/book/show/17679544-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=all-the-wrong-choices">all-the-wrong-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=yabc">yabc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=cool-author">cool-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-really-enjoyed-it">i-really-enjoyed-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=gave-away">gave-away</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581913810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3533686178228355310">You know what? Julie Kagawa is an evil genius. If that wasn't evident with the ending in <em>The Iron Queen</em> or even with <em>The Immortal Rules</em>, she definitely drove the point home with <em>The Iron Traitor</em>'s ending. I'm a little stunned this time around because I'm left wondering how she'll manage to end this thing in the next book. You'll have to excuse me if this review seems a little scattered, but the last few pages blew my little socks off into next Tuesday.<br/><br/>It's interesting that I'd have such a strong</span>
  <span id="freeText3533686178228355310" style="display:none">You know what? Julie Kagawa is an evil genius. If that wasn't evident with the ending in <em>The Iron Queen</em> or even with <em>The Immortal Rules</em>, she definitely drove the point home with <em>The Iron Traitor</em>'s ending. I'm a little stunned this time around because I'm left wondering how she'll manage to end this thing in the next book. You'll have to excuse me if this review seems a little scattered, but the last few pages blew my little socks off into next Tuesday.<br /><br />It's interesting that I'd have such a strong reaction to this installment because for the majority of the novel, I didn't feel it was as strong as Kagawa's previous works. The tone is more subdued, the witty banter is not as frequent and the overall novel just feels, for a lack of a better word, low. In hindsight, I guess that all makes sense because THAT ENDING. But it's also more than that, I realize. I knew this novel carried heavy implications for the characters. The title itself clearly gave that away as did the foreboding mannerisms of the original trio: Ash, Puck and Meghan. However, even going in knowing this, I'm still impressed that Kagawa <em>went</em> there. Brutally.<br /><br />I realize that this review is not being very helpful, so allow me to backtrack and give you a little something about the book. But it's probably not a good idea to read the rest of this review if you haven't read <em>The Lost Prince</em>.<br /><br />What I loved:<br /><br />As usual, Kagawa writes fun, relatable characters. I always know when I pick up one of her books that I'm going to laugh and fall in love with her cast. It's unavoidable and lovely. Ethan just wants a normal life with his girlfriend, Kenzie, the girl who is dying. He'd like nothing more for the fey to leave him and, more importantly, Kenzie alone. But Kenzie wants to live the rest of her life free from restrictions and craves the adventures the Nevernever provides. After trying his hardest to keep her away from Their world, they set out to look for Keirran, who has not returned to the iron realm after their last adventure. As always, there is a prophecy involved that neither Ethan or Keirran is aware of, one that has the potential to bring an end to everything. Ominously awesome, right?<br /><br />I loved Keirran especially. He's mysterious, broken, tortured and b-b-bad to the bone. Well, not really that last one, but I just wanted an excuse to say that. That is, unfortunately, the impression that he gives everyone, including Ethan, who internally struggles with his feelings of both resentment and family duty. The dynamic between Keirran and Ethan allowed for two deeper messages in the storyline, more so than I remember in Kagawa's other novels.<br /><br /><strong>1. How far do you go to help out a family member? </strong>There's no doubt that Ethan has the most to lose and little to gain from helping Keirran. Ethan blames Keirran's existence for the reason why he lost his sister Meghan to the Nevernever. Interestingly, while he remains deeply bitter about the ordeal, he always comes through for Keirran when he needs the help, even against better judgement.<br /><br /><strong>2. How do you let the one you love go?</strong> What I didn't expect to find in this spin-off was the underlying message of letting loved ones go. Ethan and Keirran aren't so different. They are both outsiders and in love with girls who are terminally ill. It's a terrible situation to see one character in, let alone two. (In case you missed it, please refer to my second sentence: Julie Kagawa is an evil genius.) The difference between the two guys is their readiness to let their love interests go. I'm not entirely convinced that Ethan is ready, but there are certain lines he has made clear he won't cross, even if that means prolonging Kenzie's life. The same can't be said for Keirran, who would destroy the world if that meant he could spend just an hour more with Annwyl.<br /><br />There's no doubt in my mind that the next book will make me cry a river, but I'm left wondering: At whose loss? How can any of this possibly end well? At least with <em>The Iron Fey</em> series, you had an idea of how things <em>could</em> conclude, though, of course, Kagawa didn't go that route.  But with <em>The Call of the Forgotten</em>, I'm mystified and worried because THAT ENDING. There's only one thing left I can do: Hold out until the next book and hope my heart can take whatever Kagawa decides to dish.<br /><br /><em>*ARC was received from YABC and the HarlequinTeen. Thank you! No monies or gifts were exchanged for this review. I am genuinely a Kagawa fangirl!</em><br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3533686178228355310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1711372349" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711372349" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711372349?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=charismatic-characters">charismatic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=interesting-villains-antiheroes">interesting-villains-antiheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=intriguing-world-building">intriguing-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=underrated-gems">underrated-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-reads-2016">great-reads-2016</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711372349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14680553884206859099"><b>*4,5/5 stars*</b><br/><br/>Firstly, Ash is still the best. Sigh. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>“A silhouette was striding down the center of the road, heading for the alley we’d just vacated. Lean, tall, a long black coat rippling behind him, he was instantly recognizable. Even from this distance, I could see the glow of his sword, blue-black and deadly, and the glint of a cold silver eye.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Now, I'm not going to bore you with my fangirling of this perfect male specimen, and onto the actual review ➵<br/><br/>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</span>
  <span id="freeText14680553884206859099" style="display:none"><b>*4,5/5 stars*</b><br /><br />Firstly, Ash is still the best. Sigh. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“A silhouette was striding down the center of the road, heading for the alley we’d just vacated. Lean, tall, a long black coat rippling behind him, he was instantly recognizable. Even from this distance, I could see the glow of his sword, blue-black and deadly, and the glint of a cold silver eye.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Now, I'm not going to bore you with my fangirling of this perfect male specimen, and onto the actual review ➵<br /><br />⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Wow! That ending was so evil (and clever) from Julie Kagawa! For some reason, although Julie is known for writing genius plot-twists and breaking the hearts of her readers on a daily basis, I didn't expect <i>Call of the Forgotten</i> to take this heartbreakingly cruel route. And how I was wrong, because Julie did it once again!<br /><br />One of the best things about all Kagawa's books are her amazing characters AND the imaginative world-buildings she creates. I love the unique world of <i>The Iron Fey</i>. I love Nevernever, all the courts (Summer, Winter, Iron) and how the world is nicely immersed in an actual faery mythology. The descriptions of the world and its creatures were so beautiful, magical and lively.<br /><br />While most of the characters in this spin-off series didn't shine for me as much as the ones from the original series - <i>The Iron Fey</i>, there is one character which does interest me (but don't mistake it for love, it's more like a fascination) in <i>Call of the Forgotten</i>. And that is Keirran. He isn't exactly a lovable character, he has some problems, messes things up and makes impulsive decisions. He's a tormented, broken soul and on his good way to be a villain. Maybe.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Be careful with that one," he said in a lower voice. "You saw what happened tonight. It was not only your darkness rising to the surface. And anger is not the only emotion that can force us to consider terrible things. There is only so much a soul can take before it is broken."</b>
</i><br /><br />There are also the differences and similarities between Keirran and the main protagonist, Ethan. Both of them have girls they love and would do anything for, and both of them have girls who are, although in a different ways, dying. <br />But Ethan has his limits, there are some things he knows are wrong and some lines he wouldn't cross, even for Kenzie. Destroying the world is one of them. <br />Keirran, on the other hand, can't stop until Annwyl is safe, he wouldn't stop before anything to save her. Even if it means a betrayal.<br /><br />With this series, I'm not sure how things would end. If there is even a chance of at least some of the main characters making it out alive, and maybe it's better that way. (Yes, I'm nice person like that.) But I hope that my babies - Ash, Puck, Meghan and Grimalkin (Well, I don't actually fear for Grimalkin. He's a cat after all. The silly fae and humans can't reach his level of awesomeness, obviously) - from <i>The Iron Fey</i>, will be safe.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>His dark gaze met mine. “You can’t save everyone,” he said in a gentle voice. “Sometimes, you have to make the decision to let them go.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14680553884206859099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400995088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11873525847375637953"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384349415i/6855840._SX540_.png' width='395' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>His dark gaze met mine. “You can’t save everyone,” he said in a gentle voice. “Sometimes, you have to make the decision to let them go.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*Lights self on fire because of the cliffhanger* - the next book may not be able to put me out of fire (<i>wait, does that even make any sense or anything?</i>). The thing is, i freaking loved this book - enough to originally want to rate it 5 stars... so why didn't i? There are several reasons and most of them include some particu</span>
  <span id="freeText11873525847375637953" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384349415i/6855840._SX540_.png" width="395" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>His dark gaze met mine. “You can’t save everyone,” he said in a gentle voice. “Sometimes, you have to make the decision to let them go.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*Lights self on fire because of the cliffhanger* - the next book may not be able to put me out of fire (<i>wait, does that even make any sense or anything?</i>). The thing is, i freaking loved this book - enough to originally want to rate it 5 stars... so why didn't i? There are several reasons and most of them include some particular characters and some points of the story. Which is why i took 0.5 stars for it (but it was definitely better than the first book).<br><br>I couldn't wait for this sequel to come out, and as soon as i saw it was out, i was so happy that i just had to start reading it right away. Generally, i was not disappointed, it was strong sequel and not just a bridge book. It was full of action and idioticness and crazyness, and scary parts and so on and on...<br><br>Unfortunately, the killer ending almost slaughtered my feels, and the next book, which i btw hope won't be the last too, cannot come out fast enough.<br><br><blockquote> <b>► STORY</b>: </blockquote><br><br>Story continues where it left off in the first book... But some time later... Ethan returned to school and life there was the same as it was before. Until he finds out that his actions and "adventure" lead Kenzie straight into a hospital bed... But, his life gets even messier when he goes to find Keirran, who went missing - with one goal in mind - to find a cure for Annwyl who is slowly fading into nothingness To make things worse, the forgotten are slowly rising and it threatens all the worlds. But no one is realizing it...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724014.Iron_s_Prophecy__The_Iron_Fey___4_5_" title="Iron's Prophecy (The Iron Fey, #4.5) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Prophecy</a> you know why it wasn't right for Keirran and Ethan to meet each other. This time, you will understand why.<br><br><blockquote> <b>► CHARACTERS</b>: </blockquote><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Ethan &amp; Kenzie</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br><b> Ethan </b> still struggles between hate toward all Fey and helping out his nephew Keirran. He just wants to do what is right, but sometimes doing the right thing may cost him everything. Ethan is the same character as before, although i have to say that he improved a lot. At least he is more open up with Kenzie and he tries his best. And his relationship with Kenzie is interesting, and their interactions are amusing as always. He may have overreacted sometimes, even though he had only best intentions in mind, but some of these actions made him look selfish - but, he redeemed himself.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> I swallowed hard. “I promise,” I said, holding her gaze. “From now on, I won’t ever try to keep you away. I’ll still probably be insanely paranoid and overprotective, but if you want to march into the Nevernever and wave a stick at a dragon, I won’t try to stop you.”<br>She raised a disbelieving eyebrow, a faint smile crossing her face. “Really? You won’t try to stop me at all.”<br>“Nope. I’ll just be sure to stand in front of the dragon with a shield when it tries to cook you.”<br>The smile broke through. “I think you have the roles backward, tough guy. Of the two of us, who’s more likely to go waving their sticks at a dragon?”<br>“Hey, I have swords now. If I’m going to be picking a fight with a dragon, you can be sure it’s not going to be with a stick.”<br>“Ethan?”<br>“Yeah?”<br>“Shut up and kiss me.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Kenzie is the true spotlight of this book. This woman is amazing character. She wants to live her life the way she wants it to be, and for everything to be on her terms. She does not agonize over her sickness, she is quite aware of what is going to happen to her - but she never stops being optimistic and wonderful. She rises up the whole atmosphere, and Kenzie is worth it. Because she is strong,brave and kind. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Keirran &amp; Annwyl</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>Their relationship and love was kind of flat out for me. Probably because it was written off pages, and we didn't really see them interact so much... All we know is that Keirran "loves" Annwyl enough to litterally DO EVERYTHING if its going to save her. Which is why i don't like him anymore. There are bounds you can and can not cross. <br><br><i>
  <b>Serious – really - spoilers:</b>
</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ ARE YOU SURE, I AM TALKING ABOUT BIG SPOILERS <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And i will probably hate him because he killed Ethan, to save Annwyl...I don't know if i should hate him for saving the one he loves, but he did it in cold blood and also unleashed ALL the forbidden... Now they can return in full form and the Veil is thorn, as far as i have understood. He did something completely undespicable for someone he loved to live. He went dark side and i dont like that at all. The worst thing is that he is going to have some kind of redemption and he is going to get HEA. Well, i hope he doesn't. He doesn't deserve it for what he has done. Unless Kagawa convinces me that it is alright to forgive him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>The old quartet: Meghan, Ash and Puck &amp; Grimalkin</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>Ofc ALL OF THEM ARE BACK. Meghan and Ash appear only for a few pages, but Grimalkin and Puck stayed far more. Oh, i cannot explain how much i love Puck and his comments, and how much i love that Meghan got stronger, and that she is not the same mindless and naive girl she was before. Ash irritated me (what can i do, i started to hate him after the first book, and i don't really understand how he had changed, because he didn't).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote> <b>► OVERALL</b>: </blockquote><br><br><b>I.enjoyed.it.so.damn.much.</b> And i loved it although the certain things like Keirran and the relationship between him and Annwyl put me off, but definitely looking forward to the next book. I just can't wait.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
<b>► REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b> </blockquote><br><br>◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322866162" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611328705" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter's Passage (The Iron Fey #1.5) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322866217" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Daughter (The Iron Fey, #2) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322866245" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen (The Iron Fey, #3) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610961346" rel="nofollow noopener">Summer's Crossing (Iron Fey, #3.5) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322866344" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Knight (Iron Fey, #4) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610961362" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron's Prophecy (The Iron Fey, #4.5) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400995065" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Lost Prince (The Iron Fey: Call of the Forgotten, #1)</a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400995088" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Iron Traitor (The Iron Fey: Call of the Forgotten, #2)</a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752613874" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Iron Warrior (The Iron Fey: Call of the Forgotten, #3) </a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>

<div id="review_389484322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389484322" />
    <a title="Michele (Reading Lark/CanadianTwiMom)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom"><img alt="Michele (Reading Lark/CanadianTwiMom)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413809734p2/3239811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389484322?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michele (Reading Lark/CanadianTwiMom)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michele (Reading Lark/CanadianTwiMom)" href="/user/show/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom">Michele (Reading Lark/CanadianTwiMom)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210916" href="/book/show/17679544-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=favourite-epic">favourite-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=fey-faeries">fey-faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=cliffhanger-ending">cliffhanger-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389484322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12794120565250035717">My review can also be found at Reading Lark: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readinglark.blogspot.ca/2013/09/book-review-iron-traitor.html'>http://readinglark.blogspot.ca/2013/0...</a><br/><br/>I never thought I'd ever...EVER...want to throw a Julie Kagawa book against the wall...The Eternity Cure came so close...but this...THIS...nearly left my fingers. Not because I hated it but because I loved the story SO much and yet, in the last two pages of the book, Julie proceeded to tear my heart out and eat it for dinner. Yes...the dreaded cliffhanger that Julie dreamed up in this one was a doozie.<br/><br/>So...the q</span>
  <span id="freeText12794120565250035717" style="display:none">My review can also be found at Reading Lark: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readinglark.blogspot.ca/2013/09/book-review-iron-traitor.html">http://readinglark.blogspot.ca/2013/0...</a><br /><br />I never thought I'd ever...EVER...want to throw a Julie Kagawa book against the wall...The Eternity Cure came so close...but this...THIS...nearly left my fingers. Not because I hated it but because I loved the story SO much and yet, in the last two pages of the book, Julie proceeded to tear my heart out and eat it for dinner. Yes...the dreaded cliffhanger that Julie dreamed up in this one was a doozie.<br /><br />So...the question that many Iron Fey fans must be asking themselves now...shouldn’t I just wait to read this when the last installment comes out so I don’t have to endure the agony of waiting a year to find out what happens next? I would answer that question with a resounding and emphatic NO!!!<br /><br />Why, you say? Well, for one, you would be missing out on Julie’s awesome story-telling for another year. And the journey to the end of this installment is full of everything we all love in Julie’s story-telling...action, adventure, romance and wonderful characters. It is totally worth enduring the cliffie! I swear!<br /><br />It’s no secret that I am a huge fan of Julie Kagawa and her stories. In my mind, they’re faery-tales for ‘big kids’. And in The Iron Traitor, Julie continues to write pure epicness. Along with the worlds and adventures we get to experience through her highly imaginative writing, her characters are the driving force for me...characters who must go through SO much STUFF, and through these experiences, they grow in the most beautiful and realistic way in a non-realistic, full-on fantasy story. Maybe they don’t always grow in the direction you want them to – initially anyway – but they grow, which is one of Julie’s greatest trademarks.<br /><br />I think you’ll agree that Julie wrote fantastic character arcs for Meghan and Ash in the previous series, and the characters in The Call of the Forgotten are no different. If you recall in the The Lost Prince, Ethan had not a chip on his shoulder, but a HUGE boulder. So angry with the fey for ripping apart his family, he perhaps drew some misconstrued conclusions over the years. As truths came to pass in this installment, and his feelings for Kenzie deepened, we saw Ethan soften just a bit while still staying true to his core. And I have to say that I LOVED seeing this side of Meghan’s ‘baby’ brother. We got glimpses of what Ethan might have been like had he not had the fey so intricately woven into his life. Who knew he had a sense of humour and can be incredibly sweet and sexy rather than always brooding and angry?<br /><br />Of course, Kenzie had a huge role to play in that. She provided another perspective in which to view the fey...and life. She continued to be a breath of fresh air, and the voice of reason in this story. I adored her character...her stubbornness (or some would say persistence) despite her fragile physical nature. Her devotion to Ethan and who she considers her friends earns her huge favourite character marks in my books! It’s no wonder Ethan’s feelings for her are getting exponentially stronger.<br /><br />We also got to know a bit more about Annwyl. Definitely one of the kinder fey-folk we’ve come to know in Julie’s books...she reminded me of another sidhe who, a long time ago and before Meghan, caught the eye of a certain icy prince; strong in mind and determination but gentle in heart and personality.<br /><br />So...perhaps was there a little bit of history repeating itself or the past influencing present events? YES to both! Lots of ties to the previous stories and their connections were stronger than ever before. I somehow knew in the back of my mind that certain things that happened in Meghan &amp; Ash’s story might influence the present...and how! Were there consequences...you bet!<br /><br />Not everyone is going to like Keirran in this installment...he perhaps came across as a bit reckless – that was no secret as you recall from the previous book – but I would argue that he was more desperate than anything else. He so desperately wanted to do the right thing and save those he loved from harm...but in his quest...things didn’t always turn out the way he had planned.<br /><br />Keirran, to me, is a good mixture of Meghan and Ash with a bit of Puck’s mischievousness thrown in for good measure. But he lacks their experience. <br /><br />Not everything was as it seemed as some answers (not all) were finally revealed pertaining to why Meghan and Ash decided to keep Ethan and Keirran apart. We always suspected it had something to do with the Oracle’s prophecy foretold in the earlier Iron Fey books. But more puzzle pieces were turned upright in this installment, revealing some of the mysteries, but not all.<br /><br />Iron Fey fans will also be happy to know that Meghan, Ash, Puck and Grim all continue to participate in this story. And I’m still swooning over Ash – especially in his role as a father.<br /><br />And so...as I closed the book – and nearly flung it against the wall – I was left with my head spinning – trying to process what just happened and try to extrapolate what might come to pass from that mother of all cliffhangers. I’ve got my theories...most of which, I’m hoping for.<br /><br />But I repeat...DO NOT wait to read this for fear of that nasty cliffie. You will be missing out on some awesome story-telling...and you just have to have faith that Julie will make it all turn out right in the end. Or at least, we can hope her editors, once again, are working to convince her of that much.<br /><br />I’d like to thank Julie Kagawa, Harlequin Teen and Netgalley for the opportunity to read The Iron Traitor before its release! You can bet I’ll be rereading this one throughout the year!<br /><br />Update (October 2015): Just completed the audiobooks of this and The Lost Prince to refresh my memory and put me back in this world I so love. The audio book was awesome and helped me to not only refresh my memory but I picked up some things I had either forgotten or missed upon my first reading. The narrator did a good job as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12794120565250035717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_753281462" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/753281462" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/753281462?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-boring">hero-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=powers">powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah">blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=decent-heroine">decent-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=emo-hero">emo-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753281462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6314047941676160184"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed this more than the first book, which I found absolutely rubbish. Not that this was great but it did manage to be somewhat entertaining in places. So yea, that was something at least.<br/><br/>-What's what: Ethan and Kenzie are back from their silly adventure in the Nevernever, but Keirran (Meghan's son/Ethan's nephew/half fae/douche) is missing. His faery girlfriend (Annwyl) is desperate to find him, she asks Ethan and Kenzie for help, they agree. Time is running out for Annwyl though, s</span>
  <span id="freeText6314047941676160184" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />I enjoyed this more than the first book, which I found absolutely rubbish. Not that this was great but it did manage to be somewhat entertaining in places. So yea, that was something at least.<br /><br />-What's what: Ethan and Kenzie are back from their silly adventure in the Nevernever, but Keirran (Meghan's son/Ethan's nephew/half fae/douche) is missing. His faery girlfriend (Annwyl) is desperate to find him, she asks Ethan and Kenzie for help, they agree. Time is running out for Annwyl though, she's fading from existence because she's been exiled from the Nevernever. Ethan and co set out to reunite Annwyl and Kierran, whilst doing so they angst, whine, and act idiotic. They eventually track him down — he's been running around trying to find a way to stop Annwyl from fading because he wuvs her so much. Bratty Kierran then teams up with Ethan and the gang, and they jump from place to place, and encounter various bad guys, learn each others secrets, generally act like silly angsty teenagers, and oh noes! Betray one another. Yea, just like Shakespeare (only lamer, stupider, and more boring).<br /><br />-Ethan was a lot more tolerable in this one. I LOATHED him in <i>The Lost Prince</i>, he was so bloody whiny and douchey. I still thought he whinged and angsted loads, but he wasn't quite as douchey as before. He also seemed a little more intelligent but maybe that was just in comparison to Kierran, who was a dumb fucky fuck. <br /><br />-Kenzie was pretty likeable, I liked that she was determined to live the rest of her life the way she wanted. She only had a short time left what with her cancer, and instead of wallowing, she embraced any chance she got at adventure. She deserved to have the last few months of her life be something memorable, epic, and worthwhile. <br />I hated how Ethan tried to stop her from getting mixed up in fae business, he knew that she wanted to experience as much as possible, and he knew that she hated people trying to control her life but he still tried to dictate her life. Yea, I get he was trying to protect her but she was dying anyway, and he was well aware of her desires to live as much as possible before she dropped dead. Why did he not get that she wanted a fantastical time instead of an unremarkable time before she died? She told him so in the first book. Ugh.<br />I know a lot of readers don't like Kenzie, but I thought she was a decent character, she was exactly what Ethan needed to get him out of his many pissy moods.<br /><br />-Ethan and Kenzie's relationship seemed so underwhelming. There was nothing really epic or romantic about them.<br /><br />-I didn't like Kierran, he had a disgusting combination of Meghan and Ash's worst traits. He was stupid, selfish, entitled, and cruel — he didn't care about anyone else as long as he got what he wanted. Yea, it was nice that he wanted Annwyl safe and healthy but that didn't mean he could behave however he wanted. He put Ethan, Kenzie and so many other people's lives at risk just so he could get his own way. And he was so fucking ungrateful about it all.<br />I knew he would turn on Ethan at the end, he chose to kill him and there's no coming back from that. I really hope Kierran's murdering ways aren't glossed over as him just not being in the right state of mind because of that dark ritual he did to save Annwyl. That would be a cop out. He killed Ethan because he was an evul, selfish bastard, and he can't be redeemed. But I'm guessing all his bad deeds will be forgotten since Ash who did much worse things than him ended up getting an undeserved HEA… So I'm sure Kierran will too. The worst that will happen to him will be that he loses Annwyl, and like Ash he'll act like a dick for centuries until some virginal teenage girl catches his eyes. So yea, I have no doubt he'll somehow get his HEA. Ugh.<br /><br />-I didn't buy the supposed epic love between Annwyl and Kierran. Probably because their romance was mostly done off page. I preferred them over Ethan and Kenzie's lacklustre relationship though. <br />Yea, I could have done with an Annwyl or Kierran POV, that way I might be more convinced of their romance — as sweet as their dedication was to each other, I just wasn't completely sold on them as a couple.<br /><br />-I was hoping for more Meghan and Puck, they were barely in it. I didn't care about Ash though, he's one the worst YA characters ever.<br /><br />-Ash was the one that started all the mess with the Forgotten/Lady, if he hadn't interfered with the balance and whatnot everything would have been fine. But because Ash was a selfish git, and did whatever he pleased, he fucked up the fae way and caused the Forgotten fae problem. If anyone should end up dead to restore the balance, it should be him.<br /><br />-What's the difference with mortal-Ash and fey-Ash?! He hasn't changed at all — he still has the same powers, he's still ageless, he's still just as strong and respected as before. What was the point of his supposed transformation when he hasn't changed at all?!<br /> <br />-Ethan's mum was quite annoying. Yea, she was still grieving for Meghan but she could have been a little more supportive of Ethan.<br /><br />-Razor was the best character, he was so funny.<br /><br />-I really hope Ethan doesn't turn into a fae of some sort.<br /><br />-I wasn't impressed with the cliffhanger… It's so bloody obvious that Ethan will survive… that necklace and/or the person on the horse will save him somehow. And no doubt Kierran will learn his lesson, and he'll be forgiven everything. Ugh.<br />I think Kenzie will die and Ethan will move on… I hate all these female characters that just end up dead so they can teach the hero some important lesson about life or something. Ugh.<br /><br />All in all, <i>The Iron Traitor</i> was mostly unremarkable - Ethan somewhat improved as a narrator, but the plot was still repetitive and dull, and most of the characters were unlikeable. I'll probably be reading the next book but only because I'm attached to the world and certain characters (Meghan, Kenzie, and Puck).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6314047941676160184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_388129243" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388129243" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388129243?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210916" href="/book/show/17679544-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=owned-arcs">owned-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388129243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14955867574954354975">I have finished the book around a month or two ago when I got my dirty paws on the silvery ARC. And since then, considering how my mind tends to deceive me into remembering every little thing, I still am overwhelmed by the emotion The Iron Traitor left in its aftermath. <br/><br/>In a very rare occasion I end up liking all the characters in a book, and it was one case where I felt connected with each of the four MCs. I felt their ego, their sentiment, their anger and desperation, love and hatred. I wanted</span>
  <span id="freeText14955867574954354975" style="display:none">I have finished the book around a month or two ago when I got my dirty paws on the silvery ARC. And since then, considering how my mind tends to deceive me into remembering every little thing, I still am overwhelmed by the emotion The Iron Traitor left in its aftermath. <br><br>In a very rare occasion I end up liking all the characters in a book, and it was one case where I felt connected with each of the four MCs. I felt their ego, their sentiment, their anger and desperation, love and hatred. I wanted to cry with Kenzie, slap some senses into Ethan, both kiss and kick Kierran at the same time for his desperation (which was stupid but brave) and hold Annwyl from fading. <br><br>I felt a lot of thing and they are ineffable. I’m not sure how to put them in words.<br><br>The story began with Ethan and Kenzie, back in his normal life, was trying to make through it. Situation worsened when Kenzie’s health started to degrade due to her cancer. Ethan soon got a surprise visit (and warning) from his sister Meghan and Annwyl regarding Kierran. On the other hand Kierran was on a hell bent mission to find a cure to stop Annwyl from fading. . So once again Ethan was pulled into an unwanted quest to help Annwyl and stop Kierran from making a serious mistake before it was too late.<br><br>A character can truly be judged based on their action and reaction in different situations. I’m glad that Miss Kagawa did something like that, by putting Ethan and Kierran in situations similar to each other. Both were on the brink of losing their love. And where Kierran could go to any extent to save his, Ethan would rather cope with it than bargaining with faeries. <br><br>Here comes the difference between them, and I accept, until this point, I was leaning towards Kierran, despite his decisions were thoughtless and actions desperate, but all he did, he did them for Annwyl. It was the madness of unconditional love, the heat, the passion and the intensity that drove him out his senses. And I don’t blame him for this. But…but until the very end, he truly crossed the line between thinkable and unthinkable, sanity and insanity. Where I rather felt pity for him than anger. <br><br>Ethan showed much more maturity than his nephew. He knew the cost and consequences that might led to further trouble. <br><br><i>I wish I could, I thought, closing my eyes. I wish there was some way, some bargain or deal or contract, to make you well again, but I know the rules. Nothing is free. Magic and power always come with a price. And maybe that’s selfish and paranoid, but I’m not willing to pay that price, or have you pay that price. Not yet. Not when there’s still a chance you could be okay without it.</i><br><br>My likeness for Ethan was not an easy one. It came with difficulties. And I took time to understand him. He was a multi-layered character, a whirlwind whose thoughts spun beneath coats of dust. He was angsty, angry, frustrated. He knew he was losing Kenzie, the pain was eating him away, yet he was trying to contend with it rather than making some stupid, instant decision that might cost a lot higher than he was ready to pay. <br><br>I have not much to say about Kenzie and Annwyl. I have always viewed Annwyl as a gentle, fragile summer girl, but the strength inside really amazed me. She stood up to Kierran for the sake of his own good which he was too blind to see. And Kenzie, brave as ever, remained pretty much same. <br><br>The world building, as usual, was lurid, cinematic. It was my sixth escapade to Never-never and like every other of my visits, it was a unique experience. The iron traitor was fast paced, action packed little read. I lost the track of time while reading. I was so devoured into pages. <br><br>Like I always say, countless times, that Julie Kagawa is one of my all-time favourite authors, and I will read anything by her.<br><br><br>I hate that ending...so so so fucking hate that cliffhanger. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380387074ra/746845.gif" width="500" height="213" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tell me, how am I supposed to take all these e..emotion. Love. Anger. Hate. Throwing me from one peak to another.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380387074ra/746846.gif" width="500" height="307" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>23-08-2013 : I got my copy today. I got my copy. Yes, you world. be jealous. <br><br>The Title is release. Holly mother of ...............I'm speechless <br>But the cover...ummm...is that Keirran on the cover? He looks creepy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14955867574954354975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3085659232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
