<div id="review_1596157565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1596157565" />
    <a title="Sinead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13986510-sinead"><img alt="Sinead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602449961p2/13986510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1596157565?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sinead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sinead" href="/user/show/13986510-sinead">Sinead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=heartbreakingly-romantic">heartbreakingly-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=un-put-down-able">un-put-down-able</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=all-the-feels">all-the-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=sad">sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1596157565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2270535470781025776">This was a good book. Let me put that out there. It was really enjoyable, the cast of characters was great to read, and the story was exciting. Julie Kagawa is a great author, and the faery world is something unbelievably imaginative… I just don’t feel as attached to the world as I do her Blood of Eden series.<br/><br/>In the first book, I loved Ethan’s narrative and how different it was to Meghan’s. He was the grouchy teenager who just wanted the fey to leave him alone. But after his unwanted adventure w</span>
  <span id="freeText2270535470781025776" style="display:none">This was a good book. Let me put that out there. It was really enjoyable, the cast of characters was great to read, and the story was exciting. Julie Kagawa is a great author, and the faery world is something unbelievably imaginative… I just don’t feel as attached to the world as I do her Blood of Eden series.<br /><br />In the first book, I loved Ethan’s narrative and how different it was to Meghan’s. He was the grouchy teenager who just wanted the fey to leave him alone. But after his unwanted adventure with Keirran and Kenzie, he’s become more accepting in his role in the fey world, even though he would rather not be involved in their world at all. He isn’t as grouchy and angry in this book as he was in the first one, but his narrative was still really great. And I loved his growing relationship with Kenzie. Despite only knowing each other for about a week, their relationship was real and so strong. Ethan just wants to protect Kenzie from the dangers of the fey, and Kenzie’s stubborn and fearless attitude keeps rebutting him. They were definitely my favourite part.<br /><br />However, it was really Keirran who caught my attention in this book. We found out that he and Annywl shared a deep and powerful love in The Lost Prince, despite it being forbidden. But with Annwyl fading due to being exiled, Kierran is willing to risk just about anything to keep her around, and he broke my heart and angered me at the same time. The hardest thing is to let someone you love go, and Kierran just isn’t able to do that. He ends up making some very questionable decisions and meddles in dark magic, which really made me worry about his character and what would happen to him. <br /><br />The concept of this book was Ethan and Kenzie helping Kierran’s quest to save Annwyl. But Kierran’s actions and choices here really made me lose faith in his character. I loved him in The Lost Prince; he was funny and entertaining and as much of a warrior as his father. And even though he still retained those traits here, I felt disappointed in the lengths he went in this book, even going as far as to threaten Ethan and Kenzie’s lives, despite how willing they were to stick with Kierran until the end. Kenzie, especially, wouldn’t let him do anything alone. Towards the end even Ethan begins to doubt his trust in his nephew – but will stick with him to stay by Kenzie’s side. <br /><br />Despite the disappointment of Kierran’s character, I still enjoyed this book. Kagawa’s faery world is something amazing, and so imaginative. I just love it. And we get supporting/cameo roles of Ash, Puck and Grimalkin as well, which is always great to see. I’d love to see Puck and Grim more often, but I understand this isn’t their story; their adventure has ended. And seeing Ash as a father was pretty great, I won’t lie. Now to see Meghan be a mom! <br /><br />ALSO: THAT ENDING.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2270535470781025776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_409531538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409531538" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4278653-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533277463p2/4278653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409531538?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/4278653-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210916" href="/book/show/17679544-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4278653-rebecca?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4278653-rebecca?shelf=out-in-2013">out-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409531538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2678431530407744789">As I've said many times before, Julie Kagawa is one of my all time favorite authors. I will gladly read anything she decides to write, and I'm really excited for the new series she has coming out soon. In the meantime, reading the Call of the Forgotten series so far has been completely enthralling. Admittedly, I was slightly less enthused about The Lost Prince as I was with all her other books, but that was mostly because I was getting used to the new characters and didn't really like Ethan much</span>
  <span id="freeText2678431530407744789" style="display:none">As I've said many times before, Julie Kagawa is one of my all time favorite authors. I will gladly read anything she decides to write, and I'm really excited for the new series she has coming out soon. In the meantime, reading the Call of the Forgotten series so far has been completely enthralling. Admittedly, I was slightly less enthused about The Lost Prince as I was with all her other books, but that was mostly because I was getting used to the new characters and didn't really like Ethan much. I found him too broody and just an iffy protagonist. <br /><br />Thankfully I didn't run into those problems too much throughout The Iron Traitor. Obviously I still miss the old stars of the Iron Fey books - Meghan, Ash and Puck - but I can't complain too much because all three do make appearances here and there and getting to see them again is like getting an unexpected treat every time. I enjoyed Ethan's point of view a lot more this time around. I'm not really sure why, he didn't seem to change that much, but I guess I mostly just liked his determination to help his friends and family. I felt sorry for him because I know how much he's just like to be normal and have nothing to do with anything Faery related. He was also kind of funny at times (though of course Puck will always be the king of humor in this world). <br /><br />There were times when I appreciated the relationship Ethan and Kenzie had, but for some reason I just don't feel as strongly about her as a person as I'd like to. Hopefully that changes in the third installment. Although Ethan is narrating, the story largely focuses on Kierran and his insane quest to keep his Summer fey girlfriend, Anwyl, from Fading away. I have very mixed feelings about him at the moment. I wasn't surprised at first that he was going to such drastic measures to keep his love safe and alive (since, you know, Ash went on a pretty difficult quest as well, for Meghan). But time after time, things went wrong for him and only went downhill each time they tried something. By the end of the book, I couldn't believe how much trouble he had caused. From hurting himself physically to possibly starting a war, Kierran did it all. <br /><br />Also, it was pretty obvious from the title and cover that he was going to end up doing something horrible at some point. Even though I was expecting it, it still came as a slap in the face. This particular things happens at the very end, making a giant mega cliffhanger that left me enraged and a little confused. Somehow I will manage to wait a year for the next book, but I have no idea how. As far as pacing goes, I don't have any complaints. A lot was happening all the time, and of course the writing was lovely. The main thing I loved about this book was how much emotion I felt while reading it - it caused me to yell at the characters, get insanely nervous and very, very happy. A lot of it is tied to my love of the previous series, but The Call of the Forgotten can definitely hold its own. The Lost Prince felt more like a set up to what was really going to unfold, and this one was the sucker punch to the gut. <br /><br /><b>Spoilers begin here</b><br /><br />The reason I was confused about the end is I'm not positive if Ethan is really dead. I mean, having a sword run you completely through the stomach pretty much says to me that he is, but . . . I have a hard time believing it. Maybe he'll be saved somehow? Honestly, I think Ethan should have been more wary of the prophecy once he discovered what it was. Sure, Kierran was his friend and his nephew, but if I looked into the future and saw someone standing over my dead body with blood all over them, I'd at least wonder if they would betray me at some point. Still, it was extremely abrupt. It was like they were getting along fine for most of the book and then two pages before the end, Kierran just stabs him because of some prophecy the Forgotten Lady told him to save himself and Anwyl. What the heck?! I have a feeling all hell is going to break loose later on. <br /><br /><b>5 stars</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2678431530407744789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_755638999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755638999" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755638999?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Robin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755638999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14187436215650349688">There should be a warning label on some books ‘SERIOUS CLIFF HANGER’ this, if you haven’t guessed is one of those books.<br/><br/>I have enjoyed all of the Iron Fey books and The Iron Traitor is no exception to that. Julie Kagawa is doing a great job of showing us two ways to deal with what is ultimately the same problem. Both Ethan and Keirran are in love with girls who are most likely doomed to die soon. How they deal with the situation is completely different. While Ethan is about support and living ev</span>
  <span id="freeText14187436215650349688" style="display:none">There should be a warning label on some books ‘SERIOUS CLIFF HANGER’ this, if you haven’t guessed is one of those books.<br /><br />I have enjoyed all of the Iron Fey books and The Iron Traitor is no exception to that. Julie Kagawa is doing a great job of showing us two ways to deal with what is ultimately the same problem. Both Ethan and Keirran are in love with girls who are most likely doomed to die soon. How they deal with the situation is completely different. While Ethan is about support and living every moment with Kenzie to its fullest Keirran is bound and determined to make any deal and pay any price to save the Summer Girl he is in love with.<br /><br />I hated Ethan for most of the last book he was broody and a little whiney. But I liked him so much more in the Iron Traitor. He has really stepped it up and with Kenzies help has accepted that the Fey will always be a part of his world. He has a few very flawed moments but all and all he was a much more likable individual in this story.<br /><br />Keirran on the other hand I wanted to smack most of the time. He made rash decisions, did stupid things and had moments of great selfishness and cruelty. He exhibited the worst traits of Meghan and Ash with the only redeeming quality being that everything he was trying to do was for the girl he loved.<br /><br />There were great betrayals and based on the title you would think I would have expected some of them but a few caught me off guard. All of the characters transformed and became more three dimensional in this story, but it is a darker tale that seems to have little hope at the end of the tunnel for some of the characters.<br /><br />Puck was able to add a little humor and after reading all of the Iron Fey series I really hoped that perhaps Keirran would have asked his father for help. If anyone would have known a way to possibly save Keirran and Annwyl it seems that Ash and Maghan would have been the go to people to ask for help. <br /><br />There is heaps of drama and things look really bad for all those involved. I can’t wait to see how this story plays out in the end as for everyone. As is it seems like there will not be a lot of Happily Ever Afters to go around and the prophecy that everyone has tried so hard to save Ethan from might have found him anyway.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14187436215650349688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_736217818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/736217818" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736217818?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210916" href="/book/show/17679544-the-iron-traitor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736217818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2621012709962605061"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Dude, that ending. That cliffhanger (but a darned good one). I think this series is shaping up to be a new favorite for me, and I loved this book, but I just have to say two things in the aftermath of reading this book:One: Keirran's an idiot. Two: Poor Ethan.<br/> <br/><b>Full review:</b><br/> <br/>I'm loving the "Call of the Forgotten" series so far - Julie Kagawa has such an eye for building the realm of the Fey as well as presenting characters that are intriguing to follow in the conflicts presented </span>
  <span id="freeText2621012709962605061" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Dude, that ending. That cliffhanger (but a darned good one). I think this series is shaping up to be a new favorite for me, and I loved this book, but I just have to say two things in the aftermath of reading this book:One: Keirran's an idiot. Two: Poor Ethan.<br /> <br /><b>Full review:</b><br /> <br />I'm loving the "Call of the Forgotten" series so far - Julie Kagawa has such an eye for building the realm of the Fey as well as presenting characters that are intriguing to follow in the conflicts presented in the world.  "The Iron Traitor" is a strong follow-up to "The Lost Prince" - providing a compelling narrative that carried me all the way through to the end, and lending into a follow-up that's sure to have much momentum to carry forward as the series continues.<br /> <br />This book picks up a little bit after the events of "The Lost Prince", and I have to say that Ethan's prejudices against the fey are much less than they were in the previous novel, though he still has his respective insecurities.  Following up, authorities and peers alike question where Ethan disappeared to for a time with Kenzie (such is the lament of one who isn't born with fey blood, as Ethan notes - you can disappear, but people will wonder where you are).   Ethan isn't just worried about Kenzie in what transpires shortly after they return, but he also comes across alarming news about Keirran, who has disappeared from the Fey realm.  Worried that Keirran may act in desperation over a lover who's existence is being erased, Ethan decides to go back into the world of the Fey to find him.  Though Ethan has more ties to events than he even knows, and it may prove disastrous for him.<br /> <br />From reading this book, I'll admit I'm enjoying following Ethan's character quite a bit. He's a flawed character, but I'll admit it's easy to care about what he thinks and see how he feels within all the events and revelations that are handed down to him. I followed his perspective well.  While there are focuses on the romantic elements between him and Kenzie (and even Keirran and his beloved), the story's more action oriented and focused on the clashes between the ever-present tensions of the realms of the Fey and the real world.  I appreciated even seeing more of the familiar faces from the last series - including Puck and Grim, who have more focused roles in this story than perhaps the former.  (Megan and Ash make brief appearances, and both are very significant to the route of the plot events.)<br /> <br />I will admit that I had an idea of where the story would go after a time when the foreshadowing measures started playing into Ethan's role and clashes with Keirran, but I still didn't expect the ending to hit as much as it did.  Keirran's motivations are clear-cut, I understood his flaws as well - even in the realm of his desperation and darkness, but it didn't keep me from raging (at him) when the ending of this novel came.  It's a great cliffhanger, though I'll admit it makes me curious to see where Kagawa will take it, for what also transpires with Ethan especially.<br /> <br />It's a novel that I would highly recommend, and I'm definitely looking forward to the next book.  Great points of humor, action, adventure, romance, and palpable stakes.<br /> <br />Overall score: 4.5/5 stars<br /> <br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher Harlequin Teen.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2621012709962605061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1379186885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379186885" />
    <a title="Dark Sith Lordette Jennymort ♔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35147071-dark-sith-lordette-jennymort"><img alt="Dark Sith Lordette Jennymort ♔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573853652p2/35147071.jpg" /></a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer718646504" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16706957872257111650">Revised Review:<br/>The Iron Traitor is gripping, intense and shocking. After his journey into the land of the fey, Ethan just wants to get back to normal. However, normal for Ethan is difficult for a former loner with a bad reputation trying to see his girlfriend Kenzie who he is forbidden to see. When Ethan’s nephew Keirran goes missing and may be on the verge of doing something unthinkable and dangerous to save his own love, Ethan, Kenzie and Annwyl go in search of him before its too late. Secrets</span>
  <span id="freeText16706957872257111650" style="display:none">Revised Review:<br>The Iron Traitor is gripping, intense and shocking. After his journey into the land of the fey, Ethan just wants to get back to normal. However, normal for Ethan is difficult for a former loner with a bad reputation trying to see his girlfriend Kenzie who he is forbidden to see. When Ethan’s nephew Keirran goes missing and may be on the verge of doing something unthinkable and dangerous to save his own love, Ethan, Kenzie and Annwyl go in search of him before its too late. Secrets are revealed, choices are made and sides are chosen as darkness approaches and the fate of both worlds hangs in the balance. The Iron Traitor is filled with action, adventure, tension, romance, shock, and the most jaw dropping cliffhanger I have ever read.<br><br>Ethan and Kenzie have returned home, faced the consequences after being missing and try to return to a normal life. However, that is impossible when the fey are involved and Ethan is forbidden to see Kenzie by her father. When Ethan learns that Keirran has disappeared, he fears that Keirran has returned to the Forgotten Queen and is joined by Kenzie and Annwyl to find him before he does anything stupid. However, Ethan is followed and threatened by a faerie known as the Thin Man, who wants to fix a mistake that was made in the past that allowed the Forgotten Queen to exist as well as to stop a prophecy from coming true. During Ethan’s search for Keirran, he discovers secrets that were kept from him and the prophecy that connects him and Keirran that could change the fate of the Nevernever.<br><br>Upon finding Keirran, they learn that he is on a mission of his own to find a way to stop Annwyl’s fading and is willing to do whatever it takes, no matter the cost. With a temporary solution that has dangerous side effects, their only hope is to remove Annwyl’s banishment leaving Ethan and group to travel back into the Nevernever. There they face impossible tasks and Keirran’s behavior worsens with every passing second putting everyone at risk. When the Queen of the Forgotten summons Keirran again, Ethan follows only for both to discover something so shocking that it puts both worlds in the balance.<br><br>Ethan and Kenzie remain great characters. I love them and the romance between them. The situation with Annwyl made me sad. Kierran was infuriating. While his intentions were good, his actions have created more harm than good and put everything and everyone at risk. The ending alone made me want to slap him. The Thin Man from the Iron Knight returns and he remains creepy as ever.<br><br>Other characters from the past return as well such as our favorite trio for a short time and its great to see them again, to see how they are after the events of their story. Some characters don’t change while others have grown.<br><br>Overall, The Iron Traitor was amazing. This book was really good and I still liked it but I was frustrated with some scenes and with a few characters, mostly with Kierran. The characters are still great, the plot deepens, and some of my questions finally get answered. We finally learn how the Forgotten came back into existence and it is linked to what happened in The Iron Knight. The ending left me screaming WTF! I need the next book now.<br><br>Old Review:<br>The Iron Traitor is gripping, intense, and shocking. The book is really good and I still liked it but I was frustrated with some scenes and with a few characters, mostly with one. We learn of how the Forgotten came back into existence is explained and it is linked to what happened in The Iron Knight. Secrets are revealed, choices are made and sides are chosen as darkness approaches and the fate of both worlds hangs in the balance. The ending left me screaming WTF!<br><br>Ethan and Kenzie return home and face the consequences of being missing for a week as well as try to be normal. However, that’s impossible when the fey are involved. When Kierran goes missing and Annwyl is fading, Ethan, Kenzie and Annwyl go in search for him. During their journey, Ethan meets the Thin Man and his desire to undo a mistake and the Oracle to where Ethan learns of the prophecy that he and Kierran play major roles in. It is the same prophecy that Meghan saw from Iron’s Prophecy. Eventually they do find Kierran and learn that he is on a mission of his own; finding a way to keep Annwyl from fading. Kierran is willing to go to great lengths for her, even using dark magic that risks corrupting his soul to do so. <br><br>Ethan and Kenzie are still great characters. I love them and the romance between them. The situation with Annwyl made me sad. Kierran is infuriating. While his intends are good, his actions have created more harm and puts everything and everyone in danger.<br><br>Overall, it was really good. The characters are still great, the plot deepens and some of my questions I had from the first book get answered. The only issue I have was Kierran who at most times was just infuriating. The ending was one of the most jaw dropping cliffhangers I have ever read, leaving me utterly shocked. I cannot wait to start reading the next book.<br><br>My reaction to the ending of the book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421764101ra/13411989.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313284570" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17757911703025646407">The Iron Traitor is the second book of The Iron Fey: Call of the Forgotten series and I loved it!!<br/><br/>This is the continuation of The Iron Prince so you must read that book to understand the story. Because of this my review is spoiler free.<br/><br/>What did I like about The Iron Traitor?<br/><br/>I loved everything about this book!<br/><br/>The Characters<br/><br/>Ethan Chase has become my favorite YA guy! He's still the tough guy that wants to keep everyone at a distance but he is slowly opening up to people. He knows he should stay awa</span>
  <span id="freeText17757911703025646407" style="display:none">The Iron Traitor is the second book of The Iron Fey: Call of the Forgotten series and I loved it!!<br /><br />This is the continuation of The Iron Prince so you must read that book to understand the story. Because of this my review is spoiler free.<br /><br />What did I like about The Iron Traitor?<br /><br />I loved everything about this book!<br /><br />The Characters<br /><br />Ethan Chase has become my favorite YA guy! He's still the tough guy that wants to keep everyone at a distance but he is slowly opening up to people. He knows he should stay away from the NeverNever since the Fey have brought him nothing but trouble. But he follows his heart and does anything he can to help the ones he cares about. He is a true hero! Keeping Ethan in check is Mackenzie who continues to be brave despite her own problems. She and Ethan make a great team and couple. Lastly there is Keran who is willing to do anything for love. He makes some disappointing choices but I'm hoping he redeems himself in the next book.<br /><br />The Story <br /><br />The Iron Traitor picks up where the last book left off and jumps back into the action and story. Julie Kagawa created an exciting fantasy that was vivid and I was drawn in from the beginning. The story has the right balance of action, young love and conflict to keep the reader entertained and intrigued. There are surprising twists and the cliffhanger ending has me wanting more! The Iron Traitor was released in 2013 but I am so glad I read this now. I would have hated to wait so long for the 3rd book, which releases in October 2015.<br /><br />This is only my second book to read from Julie Kagawa and I absolutely love her writing. She has created a fantasy world with the right amount of details to clearly imagine it without being confused. The story flows smoothly and the characters are so well developed you will love the heroes and hate the villains. And the action scenes are so exciting you won’t be able to put the book down. I highly recommend this series to fans of adventure and fantasy.<br /><br />This book meets the COYER Summer Scavenger Hunt #53, a book with just half a face on the cover.<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer177024211805025665">It took me about 5 minutes after finishing to realize why it's called The Iron Traitor. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Love you, Keirran, but we don't kill our uncles, especially ones that have risked not only their life, but their girlfriend's, who happens to be riddled with cancer. <br/><br/>And it's so great to see that Titania is still a crazy, evil bitch. She couldn't have just cut Annwyl some slack? I was so happy to see Grimalkin though. He's so rude, but he's always around to save them, or at least to tell them </span></span>
  <span id="freeText177024211805025665" style="display:none">It took me about 5 minutes after finishing to realize why it's called The Iron Traitor. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Love you, Keirran, but we don't kill our uncles, especially ones that have risked not only their life, but their girlfriend's, who happens to be riddled with cancer. <br /><br />And it's so great to see that Titania is still a crazy, evil bitch. She couldn't have just cut Annwyl some slack? I was so happy to see Grimalkin though. He's so rude, but he's always around to save them, or at least to tell them to run when they watch danger coming <b> directly towards them. </b><br /><br />Throughout the entire book I was waiting for the cops to come and arrest Ethan. Let's see how Ethan will resurrect himself cuz we all know that it's required for him to come back.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1sW+2Gi5tD09hS7E7AIv7SpPV/DbaTgYSMCeJf9BEml4j2rJmwl44fQMzCKQdhuoV0pY3s2H5YEV1oliYTX/8Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('19JoD/k3AYHo5tTDU9AnTofmY8XRJfinT7oDSFhDx+B5mLweCofNXSFvNiUvpBML+uNs68fLJT4SrBQPxjcqeA==')})
  }
//]]>
